# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes CRD Validation to OpenAPI Schema Publishing Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a CustomResourceDefinition's validation schema is converted to an OpenAPI schema in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find Go source files implementing: the CRD validation spec, the structural schema extraction, the OpenAPI v3 schema conversion, and the API server spec endpoint publication.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully traced and documented the complete CRD validation to OpenAPI schema publishing chain in kubernetes/kubernetes. 

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings that document how a CustomResourceDefinition's validation schema is converted and published as an OpenAPI schema through the Kubernetes API server.

The chain consists of **8 key stages**:

1. **Schema Definition** - `CustomResourceValidation` with `OpenAPIV3Schema` (JSONSchemaProps)
2. **JSONSchema Conversion** - `ConvertJSONSchemaPropsWithPostProcess()` converts to go-openapi format
3. **Structural Extraction** - `NewStructural()` converts JSONSchemaProps to internal structural schema
4. **OpenAPI Conversion** - `ToKubeOpenAPI()` converts structural schema to OpenAPI spec.Schema
5. **Spec Building** - `BuildOpenAPIV2()` and `BuildOpenAPIV3()` construct complete OpenAPI specs
6. **Dynamic Management** - OpenAPI controllers watch CRDs and manage specs dynamically
7. **v2 Support** - Conversion functions for OpenAPI v2 compatibility
8. **Endpoint Publication** - `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3` HTTP endpoints serve the specs

The answer includes **13 key files**, **11 important symbols**, and **8 functions in the main chain**, with a detailed narrative explaining how each component fits into the overall pipeline.

Structural Schema Extraction**\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apiserver/schema/convert.go` implements `NewStructural()` which converts JSONSchemaProps to a structural schema representation (defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apiserver/schema/structural.go`). Structural schemas enforce Kubernetes' stricter validation invariants and are required for many features including field management and pruning.\\n\\n**4. Structural Schema to OpenAPI v3 Conversion**\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver/pkg/apiserver/schema/kubeopenapi.go` file implements the `ToKubeOpenAPI()` method on the Structural type, which converts the internal structural representation back to the standard go-openapi spec.Schema format for publication.\\n\\n**5.
